But this is the one to whom I will look : he who is humble and contrite in spirit and trembles at my word .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling at God\'s word is paired with humility and a contrite spirit as the inner posture God looks for; the trembling is located in the spirit and shows reverence that orients the whole inner person toward God\'s communication.\n\n**Heb 10:27** (G5398 foberos) [M01-F-VCG-04]\n> Heb 10:27 but a fearful expectation of judgment , and a fury of fire that will consume the adversaries .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fearful expectation of judgment is the inner experience awaiting those who sin willfully after receiving truth—an anticipatory dread lodged in the mind directed toward coming fiery condemnation.\n\n**2Cor 12:20** (G5399 fobeō) [M01-F-VCG-05]\n> 2Cor 12:20 For I fear that perhaps when I come I may find you not as I wish , and that you may find me not as you wish — that perhaps there may be quarreling , jealousy , anger , hostility , slander , gossip , conceit , and disorder .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Paul\'s fear is an anticipatory dread rooted in thought about what he may find—relational disorder and sin—engaging the mind with anxious expectation before the visit even happens.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n\n\n### 2.2 Acute Fear and Alarm\n\nAcute fear and alarm is the sudden seizing of the inner person by fright — the immediate, overwhelming response to a specific trigger. It is episodic rather than settled: it arises at a moment, floods the inner person, and governs what happens next. The trigger may be a threatening army, as when "all the men of Israel, when they saw the man, fled from him and were much afraid" at the sight of Goliath (1Sa 17:24); or it may be a supernatural encounter, as when the shepherds in the field "were filled with great fear" when the angel of the Lord appeared and the divine glory shone around them (Luk 2:9). In both cases the inner experience is the same in structure: sudden, overwhelming, immediate in its effect on the will. At the transfiguration, Mark records simply that Peter "did not know what to say, for they were terrified" (Mar 9:6) — thought and speech shut down under the force of it. Acute fear is the inner person\'s most immediate register of power encountered without preparation.\n\nThis is what distinguishes it from reverential fear, which is a settled orientation of the whole life. Acute fear and alarm is reactive and situational — it arises when something specific is encountered, subsides when the moment passes, and in Scripture is regularly the occasion for divine command: "fear not" addresses this state, not the disposition of reverential fear. It also differs from terror as overwhelming force, which emphasises what the terror does — pursuing, encircling, assaulting — rather than the reactive episode within the person who receives it. Acute fear names the inner event; terror as overwhelming force names the agent. Acute fear also extends, in the New Testament, to the social register: fear of the crowd, fear of the authorities, the suppression of honest speech under pressure of what others might do.\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.2 — Acute Fear and Alarm -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Reactive, situational fear — sudden inner state of alarm, dread, or terror triggered by specific threat, unexpected encounter, supernatural appearance, or display of divine/extraordinary power. Episodic character: arises at a moment, overwhelms the inner person, governs the will\'s immediate response. OT: dread before armies (Num 22:3; Deu 20:1-3), divine theophanies (Exo 34:30; Judg 6:23), inexplicable events (Gen 42:35). NT: disciples at Jesus walking on water, transfiguration, calmed storm, resurrection appearances. Includes social fear: fear of crowds governing rulers\' decisions, fear of the Jews suppressing speech. Reactive-and-episodic distinguishes M01-B from A\'s chronic orientation.\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Psa 25:14** (H3373 ya.re) [M01-A-VCG-03]\n> Psa 25:14 The friendship of the Lord is for those who fear him, and he makes known to them his covenant .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The fear of God positions a person for intimate covenant relationship with the Lord — those whose inner life is marked by this reverence receive God\'s friendship and knowledge of his covenant.\n\n**Jer 5:22** (H3372H ya.re) [M01-A-VCG-05]\n> Jer 5:22 Do you not fear me? declares the Lord . Do you not tremble before me ? I placed the sand as the boundary for the sea , a perpetual barrier that it cannot pass ; though the waves toss , they cannot prevail ; though they roar , they cannot pass over it .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God confronts the people\'s inner failure to fear him, pointing to the sea\'s obedient trembling before his boundary as shaming contrast; the expected inner posture is awe that recognizes God\'s sovereign ordering of creation.\n\n**Gen 9:2** (H4172B mo.ra) [M01-A-VCG-07]\n> Gen 9:2 The fear of you and the dread of you shall be upon every beast of the earth and upon every bird of the heavens , upon everything that creeps on the ground and all the fish of the sea . Into your hand they are delivered .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fear directed toward humans is placed upon every creature as a permanent condition; it shapes animals\' inner response to mankind, producing avoidance and submission.\n\n**Deu 4:34** (H4172A mo.rah) [M01-A-VCG-07]\n> Deu 4:34 Or has any god ever attempted to go and take a nation for himself from the midst of another nation , by trials , by signs , by wonders , and by war , by a mighty hand and an outstretched arm , and by great deeds of terror , all of which the Lord your God did for you in Egypt before your eyes ?\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God\'s great deeds of terror in Egypt are acts that overwhelm the will — the term names the fear-inspiring power displayed through wonders and war that demonstrated God\'s unmatched authority over nations.\n\n**Dan 2:31** (H1763 de.chal) [M01-B-VCG-01]\n> Dan 2:31 " You saw , O king , and behold , a great image . This image , mighty and of exceeding brightness , stood before you, and its appearance was frightening .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The great image\'s appearance was frightening—its exceeding brightness and might produce a visual impression that generates fear as the inner response to an overwhelming, awe-inspiring sight.\n\n**Dan 3:24** (H8429 te.vah) [M01-B-VCG-01]\n> Dan 3:24 Then King Nebuchadnezzar was astonished and rose up in haste . He declared to his counselors , "Did we not cast three men bound into the fire ?" They answered and said to the king , " True , O king ."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Startlement seizes Nebuchadnezzar at the unexpected sight of a fourth figure in the furnace—the inner jolt of the inexplicable overrides calm and produces immediate, alarmed physical movement.\n\n**Mic 7:17** (H2119B za.chal) [M01-B-VCG-01]\n> Mic 7:17 they shall lick the dust like a serpent , like the crawling things of the earth ; they shall come trembling out of their strongholds ; they shall turn in dread to the Lord our God , and they shall be in fear of you .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The nations crawl out of their strongholds in fearful retreat, shrinking like serpents—this cringing, creeping movement embodies the inner collapse of pride into abject terror before the Lord.\n\n**Mar 9:6** (G1630 ekfobos) [M01-B-VCG-01]\n> Mar 9:6 For he did not know what to say , for they were terrified .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Peter\'s inability to know what to say at the transfiguration is explained by the terror gripping the disciples; the fear so overwhelms their inner faculties that thought and speech are disabled.\n\n**Luk 2:9** (G5399 fobeō) [M01-B-VCG-01]\n> Luk 2:9 And an angel of the Lord appeared to them , and the glory of the Lord shone around them , and they were filled with great fear .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The shepherds are filled with great fear when the angel appears and the divine glory shines around them — the inner being is overwhelmed and filled to capacity by terror at the supernatural presence.\n\n**Luk 24:5** (G1719 emfobos) [M01-B-VCG-01]\n> Luk 24:5 And as they were frightened and bowed their faces to the ground , the men said to them , " Why do you seek the living among the dead ?\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The women are frightened and bow to the ground at the angelic appearance — their inner fear expresses itself in physical prostration, showing that the terror has overwhelmed both spirit and body.\n\n**Mar 4:41** (G5401 fobos) [M01-B-VCG-02]\n> Mar 4:41 And they were filled with great fear and said to one another , " Who then is this , that even the wind and the sea obey him ?"\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Great fear fills the disciples as they witness Jesus commanding wind and sea into calm; the fear is an awe-filled inner response to displayed divine power that immediately issues in questioning his identity.\n\n**Mar 9:15** (G1568 ekthambeo) [M01-B-VCG-02]\n> Mar 9:15 And immediately all the crowd , when they saw him , were greatly amazed and ran up to him and greeted him .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The crowd\'s great amazement at seeing Jesus produces an immediate physical response of running toward him; the awe-struck wonder engages both perception and body, expressing astonishment at his unexpected presence.\n\n**Act 3:11** (G1569 ekthambos) [M01-B-VCG-02]\n> Act 3:11 While he clung to Peter and John , all the people , utterly astounded , ran together to them in the portico called Solomon\'s .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The people were utterly astounded—their inner state so overwhelming that it propelled them physically to run toward Peter and John, showing astonishment as a force that drives outward movement.\n\n**Num 22:3** (H1481C gur) [M01-B-VCG-03]\n> Num 22:3 And Moab was in great dread of the people , because they were many . Moab was overcome with fear of the people of Israel .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Moab\'s dread of Israel is visceral and overwhelming — the great number of the people produced an intense inward terror in the Moabites, described as being overcome, showing fear as a paralyzing inner state.\n\n**1Sa 17:24** (H3372G ya.re) [M01-B-VCG-03]\n> 1Sa 17:24 All the men of Israel , when they saw the man , fled from him and were much afraid .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The sight of Goliath produces extreme fear that immediately overrides the will — all the men of Israel flee before the threat without deliberation, driven by overwhelming dread.\n\n**Jer 22:25** (H3016 ya.gor) [M01-B-VCG-03]\n> Jer 22:25 and give you into the hand of those who seek your life , into the hand of those of whom you are afraid , even into the hand of Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon and into the hand of the Chaldeans .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Jehoiachin is handed over to the very enemies he fears; the inner object of his dread — those whose power over him he dreads — becomes the instrument of his judgment, so that fear and fate converge.\n\n**Luk 21:9** (G4422 ptoeō) [M01-B-VCG-03]\n> Luk 21:9 And when you hear of wars and tumults , do not be terrified , for these things must first take place , but the end will not be at once ."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Jesus commands his disciples not to be terrified by wars and tumults — the inner being is not to be shaken into panic by alarming events, because such things must happen before the end comes.\n\n**Phili 1:28** (G4426 pturomai) [M01-B-VCG-03]\n> Phili 1:28 and not frightened in anything by your opponents . This is a clear sign to them of their destruction , but of your salvation , and that from God .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The believers are urged not to be frightened by opponents—the inner movement of alarm is named as something to be actively resisted, and its absence signals salvation and divine backing.\n\n**Mat 21:26** (G5399 fobeō) [M01-B-VCG-04]\n> Mat 21:26 But if we say , \' From man ,\' we are afraid of the crowd , for they all hold that John was a prophet ."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The religious leaders\' fear of the crowd\'s reaction controls their public answer about John\'s baptism; social dread of the people\'s opinion paralyzes their will and shapes their speech.\n\n**Gen 32:7** (H3372G ya.re) [M01-B-VCG-05]\n> Gen 32:7 Then Jacob was greatly afraid and distressed . He divided the people who were with him, and the flocks and herds and camels , into two camps ,\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Jacob is greatly afraid and distressed at the prospect of meeting Esau; the fear is an intense inner alarm that immediately drives strategic action—splitting his people into two camps.\n\n**Isa 43:1** (H3372G ya.re) [M01-B-VCG-06]\n> Isa 43:1 But now thus says the Lord , he who created you, O Jacob , he who formed you, O Israel : " Fear not , for I have redeemed you; I have called you by name , you are mine .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God commands Jacob \'fear not\' on the grounds of redemption and personal naming—the inner fear is to be surrendered because belonging to God (\'you are mine\') removes the ground for dread.\n\n**Isa 44:8** (H7297 ra.hah) [M01-B-VCG-06]\n> Isa 44:8 Fear not , nor be afraid ; have I not told you from of old and declared it? And you are my witnesses ! Is there a God besides me? There is no Rock ; I know not any."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Being afraid is paired with \'fear not\' and countered by God\'s long-declared word; the inner state of fright is portrayed as having no valid object once God\'s sole sovereignty is acknowledged.\n\n**1Pe 3:6** (G4423 ptoēsis) [M01-B-VCG-06]\n> 1Pe 3:6 as Sarah obeyed Abraham , calling him lord . And you are her children , if you do good and do not fear anything that is frightening .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Ptoēsis names the alarming inner fright that circumstances can provoke; Sarah\'s daughters are called not to yield to such frightening feelings, grounding courage in doing good rather than suppressing anxiety by will alone.\n\n**Psa 6:3** (H0926 ba.hal) [M01-D-VCG-01]\n> Psa 6:3 My soul also is greatly troubled . But you , O Lord — how long ?\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The psalmist\'s soul itself is greatly dismayed — the inner being, not just the body, is the seat of this profound turmoil, and it drives the anguished cry to God asking how long.\n\n**Isa 28:19** (H2113 ze.va.ah) [M01-D-VCG-01]\n> Isa 28:19 As often as it passes through it will take you; for morning by morning it will pass through , by day and by night ; and it will be sheer terror to understand the message .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Understanding the message of judgment brings sheer terror—grasping its content produces a trembling horror, making comprehension itself terrifying rather than comforting.\n\n**1Sa 14:15** (H2729 cha.rad) [M01-D-VCG-05]\n> 1Sa 14:15 And there was a panic in the camp , in the field , and among all the people . The garrison and even the raiders trembled , the earth quaked , and it became a very great panic .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling spreads through the Philistine garrison as a contagious inner panic; joined by an earthquake, it produces a total collapse of military cohesion described as a great panic.\n\n**Pro 28:22** (H0926 ba.hal) [M01-D-VCG-05]\n> Pro 28:22 A stingy man hastens after wealth and does not know that poverty will come upon him .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The stingy man hastens after wealth in inner agitation, unaware that poverty is coming; the term points to impulsive, rash inner drive rather than outward terror in this verse.\n\n**Jer 49:24** (H7374 re.tet) [M01-D-VCG-05]\n> Jer 49:24 Damascus has become feeble , she turned to flee , and panic seized her; anguish and sorrows have taken hold of her, as of a woman in labor .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Panic seizes Damascus as it turns to flee, gripping it alongside anguish and birth-pangs; the inner experience is sudden, overwhelming, and physically incapacitating, driving flight and helplessness.\n\n**Gen 27:33** (H2731 cha.ra.dah) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Gen 27:33 Then Isaac trembled very violently and said , " Who was it then that hunted game and brought it to me, and I ate it all before you came , and I have blessed him? Yes, and he shall be blessed ."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Isaac\'s great trembling names the intensity of his inner shock when he discovers he has been deceived; the trembling registers the inner disruption caused by the loss of control over the blessing.\n\n**Exo 15:14** (H7264 ra.gaz) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Exo 15:14 The peoples have heard ; they tremble ; pangs have seized the inhabitants of Philistia .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The nations tremble upon hearing of what God did at the sea; the trembling is an involuntary inner and bodily response of dread produced by hearing of overwhelming divine power directed against enemies.\n\n**Exo 15:15** (H7461A ra.ad) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Exo 15:15 Now are the chiefs of Edom dismayed ; trembling seizes the leaders of Moab ; all the inhabitants of Canaan have melted away .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling seizes the leaders of Moab upon hearing of God\'s acts; the trembling is an uncontrollable inner and physical response to news of divine power, paralyzing those who hear it.\n\n**Deu 1:29** (H6206 a.rats) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Deu 1:29 Then I said to you, \'Do not be in dread or afraid of them .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The people are told not to be in dread — the term names the inner, overwhelming terror that grips a person before a feared enemy; here it is prohibited because God himself fights for Israel.\n\n**Deu 28:66** (H6342 pa.chad) [M01-F-VCG-03]\n> Deu 28:66 Your life shall hang in doubt before you. Night and day you shall be in dread and have no assurance of your life .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Continual dread without assurance of life is a covenantal curse; the inner experience is unrelenting, consuming both night and day, with no relief or certainty of survival.\n\n**Heb 10:27** (G5398 foberos) [M01-F-VCG-04]\n> Heb 10:27 but a fearful expectation of judgment , and a fury of fire that will consume the adversaries .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fearful expectation of judgment is the inner experience awaiting those who sin willfully after receiving truth—an anticipatory dread lodged in the mind directed toward coming fiery condemnation.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n\n\n### 2.3 Boundary — Terms Held for Researcher Decision\n\nAmong the terms that appear across the fear vocabulary of Scripture, a number resist straightforward placement. They surface in the verse evidence — in contexts of alarm, amazement, anguish, and dread — but their meaning in the corpus either proved too thin to classify (all relevant verses set aside without yielding a clear inner-being sense) or raised questions that remained unresolved at the point of analysis. These terms are held pending further decision rather than assigned to one of the established characteristics. They include words for amazement and astonishment (*ta.mah*, Gen 43:33: "the men looked at one another in amazement"), for anguish that grips and will not let go (*sha.vats*, 2Sa 1:9: "anguish has seized me, and yet my life still lingers"), and for oppressive, crushing pressure (*a.qah*, Psa 55:3). Some suggest territory adjacent to dismay or anxiety; others touch the edges of wonder and shock without landing clearly inside the established forms. Their presence is acknowledged here because they are part of the lexical range from which this study\'s evidence is drawn. They are not, however, treated as fully established characteristics in the chapters that follow.\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.3 — Boundary -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Terms with empty meaning corpora (all verses set aside, no Pass A meanings) OR with analytical questions unresolved in Phase 3. Cannot be placed in a substantive sub-group from meaning corpus alone. Held for researcher decision at Phase 12 closure gate. Remain in cluster; verses where any exist route to BOUNDARY. Members: ademoneo, thambos, za.a.vah, ke.ra, mish.bar, a.qah, sha.vats, sar.ap.pim, ta.mah, sham.mah, a.ruts, pa.lats.\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Gen 43:33** (H8539 ta.mah) [M01-BOUNDARY-VCG-01]\n> Gen 43:33 And they sat before him, the firstborn according to his birthright and the youngest according to his youth . And the men looked at one another in amazement .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The brothers are struck with amazement when seated in exact birth order before Joseph; the inner state is astonished bewilderment at what they cannot explain, expressed in their mutual staring.\n\n**2Sa 1:9** (H7661 sha.vats) [M01-BOUNDARY-VCG-01]\n> 2Sa 1:9 And he said to me, \' Stand beside me and kill me, for anguish has seized me , and yet my life still lingers .\'\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The agony gripping the wounded man is an internal seizure — it has taken hold of him body and soul, making death preferable to the torment of lingering between life and death.\n\n**2Sa 22:5** (H4867 mish.bar) [M01-BOUNDARY-VCG-01]\n> 2Sa 22:5 "For the waves of death encompassed me, the torrents of destruction assailed me;\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The waves of death are described as encompassing the psalmist — the imagery of overwhelming breakers pressing in from all sides captures the total engulfment of the inner person by mortal terror.\n\n**Psa 55:3** (H6125 a.qah) [M01-BOUNDARY-VCG-01]\n> Psa 55:3 because of the noise of the enemy , because of the oppression of the wicked . For they drop trouble upon me, and in anger they bear a grudge against me .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The pressure comes from enemy oppression — the wicked drop trouble on the psalmist and bear anger against him, producing an inner sense of being crushed by hostile, relentless external force.\n\n**Dan 7:15** (H3735 ke.ra) [M01-BOUNDARY-VCG-01]\n> Dan 7:15 "As for me , Daniel , my spirit within me was anxious , and the visions of my head alarmed me .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Distress is located explicitly within Daniel\'s spirit—the visions grip the innermost self, producing an anxious, troubled state at the core of the person rather than merely an external or cognitive reaction.\n\n**Mat 26:37** (G0085 ademoneo) [M01-BOUNDARY-VCG-01]\n> Mat 26:37 And taking with him Peter and the two sons of Zebedee , he began to be sorrowful and troubled .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Jesus begins to be sorrowful and troubled in Gethsemane; the distress is a deeply agitated inner state engaging his soul as he faces the approaching suffering, manifesting as anguished heaviness of spirit.\n\n**Act 3:10** (G2285 thambos) [M01-BOUNDARY-VCG-01]\n> Act 3:10 and recognized him as the one who sat at the Beautiful Gate of the temple , asking for alms . And they were filled with wonder and amazement at what had happened to him .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Recognizing the healed man as the familiar beggar filled the crowd with wonder and amazement, showing that the inner state is triggered by the stark contrast between what they knew and what they now see.\n\n**Psa 94:19** (H8312 sar.ap.pim) [M01-F-VCG-01]\n> Psa 94:19 When the cares of my heart are many , your consolations cheer my soul .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Anxious cares multiply within the heart, but God\'s consolations restore the soul — the anxiety is located in the heart as a crowding inner burden that divine comfort directly counters.\n\n**Eze 12:18** (H1674 de.a.gah) [M01-F-VCG-01]\n> Eze 12:18 " Son of man , eat your bread with quaking , and drink water with trembling and with anxiety .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Anxiety so saturates the inner person that even the basic acts of eating and drinking cannot be done without it—it is a constant, pervasive inner dread that accompanies every moment of existence.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n\n\n### 2.4 Terror as Overwhelming Force\n\nTerror as overwhelming force is Scripture\'s name for fear when the emphasis falls not on the person who experiences it but on the power that inflicts it. Something comes upon the inner person from outside — it encircles, pursues, strips identity, paralyses the will. Job 18:11 describes the wicked man\'s fate in these terms: "Terrors frighten him on every side, and chase him at his heels." The terror here is an agent, not merely a feeling. It hunts. In the same way, God sends his terror as an advance weapon before Israel: "I will send my terror before you and will throw into confusion all the people against whom you shall come" (Exo 23:27). The inner effect in the enemies — confusion, flight, the collapse of resistance — is produced not by Israel\'s strength but by a dread dispatched by God ahead of them. This is the characteristic\'s defining feature: agency. The terror does something. It encircles (Psa 31:13), it strips a person of their identity and honour (Job 30:15), it renders armies motionless (Gen 35:5), it is projected by military empires as a form of power in itself (Eze 32:23). After the flood, God placed the dread of humanity upon all living creatures: "The fear of you and the dread of you shall be upon every beast of the earth" (Gen 9:2) — an instilled orientation in the creature, directed outward as a permanent condition.\n\nWhat distinguishes terror as overwhelming force from acute fear and alarm is the direction of attention. Acute fear is the inner event in the person startled or frightened. Terror as overwhelming force is the power that causes that event — described from the outside, with emphasis on what the terror itself does. They are complementary registers: one describes the experience, the other describes the force that shapes it.\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.4 — Terror as Overwhelming Force -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Terror characterised as active, assaulting force — something that comes upon the inner person from outside, encircles them, pursues them, or is projected by one power onto another. Distinctive: agency and force of the terror itself. It hunts (bal.la.hah, Job 18:11), encircles (ma.gor, Jer 6:25; 20:10; Lam 2:22), is sent as weapon by God (e.mah, Exo 23:27; chit.tah, Gen 35:5; pa.chad, Deu 2:25), projected by military empires (chit.tit, Eze 32:23-32). Strips identity (bal.la.hah, Job 30:15), paralyses will (chit.tah, Gen 35:5), renders enemies motionless (e.mah, Exo 15:16). The terror is often divine in origin — dread deployed as weapon. Also: awe-inspiring terror-force radiating from powerful entities (Leviathan, war horse, a.yom in Song 6:4).\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Gen 9:2** (H4172B mo.ra) [M01-A-VCG-07]\n> Gen 9:2 The fear of you and the dread of you shall be upon every beast of the earth and upon every bird of the heavens , upon everything that creeps on the ground and all the fish of the sea . Into your hand they are delivered .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fear directed toward humans is placed upon every creature as a permanent condition; it shapes animals\' inner response to mankind, producing avoidance and submission.\n\n**Deu 4:34** (H4172A mo.rah) [M01-A-VCG-07]\n> Deu 4:34 Or has any god ever attempted to go and take a nation for himself from the midst of another nation , by trials , by signs , by wonders , and by war , by a mighty hand and an outstretched arm , and by great deeds of terror , all of which the Lord your God did for you in Egypt before your eyes ?\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God\'s great deeds of terror in Egypt are acts that overwhelm the will — the term names the fear-inspiring power displayed through wonders and war that demonstrated God\'s unmatched authority over nations.\n\n**Gen 35:5** (H2847 chit.tah) [M01-C-VCG-01]\n> Gen 35:5 And as they journeyed , a terror from God fell upon the cities that were around them, so that they did not pursue the sons of Jacob .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ A God-sent terror fell upon the surrounding cities, paralyzing their will to pursue Jacob\'s sons; the inner state in the enemies is externally imposed dread that disables hostile action.\n\n**Exo 23:27** (H0367 e.mah) [M01-C-VCG-01]\n> Exo 23:27 I will send my terror before you and will throw into confusion all the people against whom you shall come , and I will make all your enemies turn their backs to you.\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God\'s terror is sent as an advance weapon — it works on enemy peoples\' inner being, throwing them into confusion and causing them to flee, so that it is God\'s dread, not Israel\'s strength, that defeats them.\n\n**Isa 19:17** (H2283 chag.ga) [M01-C-VCG-01]\n> Isa 19:17 And the land of Judah will become a terror to the Egyptians . Everyone to whom it is mentioned will fear because of the purpose that the Lord of hosts has purposed against them .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Judah becomes an object of terror to Egypt—merely mentioning it provokes fear in Egyptians because of what God has purposed against them; the terror is caused by divine intent, not Judah\'s own might.\n\n**Job 18:11** (H1091 bal.la.hah) [M01-C-VCG-02]\n> Job 18:11 Terrors frighten him on every side , and chase him at his heels .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terrors surround the wicked man on every side and pursue him relentlessly, depicting terror as an encircling, hunting force that overwhelms the inner person with no escape.\n\n**Psa 31:13** (H4032 ma.gor) [M01-C-VCG-02]\n> Psa 31:13 For I hear the whispering of many — terror on every side !— as they scheme together against me, as they plot to take my life .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The psalmist hears whispering enemies plotting against his life, and terror surrounds him on every side — this terror is the inner experience of being hunted, enclosed by threat from all directions.\n\n**Jer 8:15** (H1205 be.a.tah) [M01-C-VCG-02]\n> Jer 8:15 We looked for peace , but no good came; for a time of healing , but behold , terror .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror arrives where healing was expected; the inner experience of shattered hope turns into shock as what was anticipated — peace and recovery — is replaced by something that dismays and overwhelms.\n\n**Jer 49:16** (H8606 tiph.le.tset) [M01-C-VCG-03]\n> Jer 49:16 The horror you inspire has deceived you, and the pride of your heart , you who live in the clefts of the rock , who hold the height of the hill . Though you make your nest as high as the eagle\'s , I will bring you down from there , declares the Lord .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Edom\'s pride in its mountain strongholds was fed by the terror it inspired in others, but that very reputation deceived Edom into false security — the fear it caused others could not protect it.\n\n**Eze 32:23** (H2851 chit.tit) [M01-C-VCG-03]\n> Eze 32:23 whose graves are set in the uttermost parts of the pit ; and her company is all around her grave , all of them slain , fallen by the sword , who spread terror in the land of the living .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror is the power Assyria wielded over the living—it was the active force projected from her military might, now stripped away in death, where she lies powerless in the pit.\n\n**Gen 9:2** (H2844A chat) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Gen 9:2 The fear of you and the dread of you shall be upon every beast of the earth and upon every bird of the heavens , upon everything that creeps on the ground and all the fish of the sea . Into your hand they are delivered .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror is an instilled inner disposition placed upon all animals toward humanity after the flood, making every creature fear humans as a divinely ordered reality.\n\n**Psa 55:4** (H0367 e.mah) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Psa 55:4 My heart is in anguish within me; the terrors of death have fallen upon me .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror is located in the heart — the terrors of death fall upon the psalmist, causing inner anguish so intense it is felt as a physical collapse within the chest.\n\n**Pro 18:7** (H4288 me.chit.tah) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Pro 18:7 A fool\'s mouth is his ruin , and his lips are a snare to his soul .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The verse describes self-destructive ruin without using the term\'s direct inner-being content; terror here is implied as outcome—the fool\'s own speech ensnares his soul, making his mouth the instrument of his undoing.\n\n**Ecc 12:5** (H2849 chat.chat) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Ecc 12:5 they are afraid also of what is high , and terrors are in the way ; the almond tree blossoms , the grasshopper drags itself along, and desire fails , because man is going to his eternal home , and the mourners go about the streets —\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terrors are in the way for the aging person approaching death; the inner experience is one of dread at life\'s journey as desire fails and the eternal home nears.\n\n**Isa 10:33** (H4637 ma.a.ra.tsah) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Isa 10:33 Behold , the Lord God of hosts will lop the boughs with terrifying power; the great in height will be hewn down , and the lofty will be brought low .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The Lord\'s terrifying power is the force by which he will cut down the proud and mighty; terror here describes the overwhelming, awe-striking quality of divine judgment that brings the lofty low.\n\n**Job 6:21** (H2866 cha.tat) [M01-C-VCG-05]\n> Job 6:21 For you have now become nothing ; you see my calamity and are afraid .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Job\'s friends are so terrified by his calamity that they become useless to him, showing terror as an inner reaction that shuts down compassionate response.\n\n**Hab 1:7** (H0366 a.yom) [M01-C-VCG-05]\n> Hab 1:7 They are dreaded and fearsome ; their justice and dignity go forth from themselves.\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The Babylonians are described as inherently terrible and fearsome, projecting an inner quality of terrifying power outward; they are dread-inspiring in themselves, a force that generates fear in all they encounter.\n\n**Heb 10:27** (G5398 foberos) [M01-F-VCG-04]\n> Heb 10:27 but a fearful expectation of judgment , and a fury of fire that will consume the adversaries .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fearful expectation of judgment is the inner experience awaiting those who sin willfully after receiving truth—an anticipatory dread lodged in the mind directed toward coming fiery condemnation.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n\n\n### 2.5 Dismay and Inner Collapse\n\nDismay is what happens to the inner person when fear has done more than alarm — when it has shattered. The person who experiences acute fear is startled, seized, driven to flight; the person in dismay cannot answer, cannot speak, cannot act. Daniel records the moment it happened to Belshazzar: "Then the king\'s color changed, and his thoughts alarmed him; his limbs gave way, and his knees knocked together" (Dan 5:6). That is dismay — the inner collapse made visible in the body. The soul itself is the site of it, as the psalmist cries: "My soul also is greatly troubled. But you, O Lord — how long?" (Psa 6:3). Scripture shows it arriving through catastrophe and overwhelming news, through grasping the content of a terrible message (Isa 28:19), through the sight of something that the mind cannot contain. It can be divinely imposed as an instrument of judgment: God declares through Jeremiah, "I will terrify Elam before their enemies" — making dismay the condition through which he breaks the will of a people (Jer 49:37). It can also spread contagiously: the panic that seized the Philistine garrison at Jonathan\'s attack moved through the camp like a wave, until it became "a very great panic" (1Sa 14:15).\n\nDismay differs from acute fear in that it describes the state *after* overwhelming fear has done its work — dissolution, not alarm. It differs from terror as overwhelming force by naming the condition in the person rather than the power pressing upon them. And it differs from trembling, which is the body\'s expression of fear: dismay is the collapse of inner coherence itself, the disabling of the faculties that normally hold the person together.\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.5 — Dismay and Inner Collapse -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Sudden dissolution of inner coherence — what happens to the inner person when shock, catastrophe, or overwhelming news shatters composure and disables capacity to function. Collapse: dismayed person cannot answer (ba.hal, Gen 45:3), cannot see (Isa 21:3), cannot speak (cha.tat, Job 32:15), cannot resist (Judg 20:41), cannot act (Jer 17:18). Visible on body: color changes (be.hal, Dan 5:6; 5:9), limbs give way, hands paralysed (cha.tat, Eze 7:27). Can be divinely imposed (ba.hal, Psa 2:5; 90:7; cha.tat, Jer 49:37), natural response to catastrophe, or inner effect of grasping terrible message (Dan 4:19; 7:15). Distinct from acute alarm (M01-B): emphasis is dissolution of inner coherence, not reactive alertness. Dismay is the state after fear has overwhelmed — the shattering, not just the shock.\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Gen 9:2** (H2844A chat) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Gen 9:2 The fear of you and the dread of you shall be upon every beast of the earth and upon every bird of the heavens , upon everything that creeps on the ground and all the fish of the sea . Into your hand they are delivered .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror is an instilled inner disposition placed upon all animals toward humanity after the flood, making every creature fear humans as a divinely ordered reality.\n\n**Psa 55:4** (H0367 e.mah) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Psa 55:4 My heart is in anguish within me; the terrors of death have fallen upon me .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror is located in the heart — the terrors of death fall upon the psalmist, causing inner anguish so intense it is felt as a physical collapse within the chest.\n\n**Pro 18:7** (H4288 me.chit.tah) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Pro 18:7 A fool\'s mouth is his ruin , and his lips are a snare to his soul .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The verse describes self-destructive ruin without using the term\'s direct inner-being content; terror here is implied as outcome—the fool\'s own speech ensnares his soul, making his mouth the instrument of his undoing.\n\n**Ecc 12:5** (H2849 chat.chat) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Ecc 12:5 they are afraid also of what is high , and terrors are in the way ; the almond tree blossoms , the grasshopper drags itself along, and desire fails , because man is going to his eternal home , and the mourners go about the streets —\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terrors are in the way for the aging person approaching death; the inner experience is one of dread at life\'s journey as desire fails and the eternal home nears.\n\n**Isa 10:33** (H4637 ma.a.ra.tsah) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Isa 10:33 Behold , the Lord God of hosts will lop the boughs with terrifying power; the great in height will be hewn down , and the lofty will be brought low .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The Lord\'s terrifying power is the force by which he will cut down the proud and mighty; terror here describes the overwhelming, awe-striking quality of divine judgment that brings the lofty low.\n\n**Psa 6:3** (H0926 ba.hal) [M01-D-VCG-01]\n> Psa 6:3 My soul also is greatly troubled . But you , O Lord — how long ?\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The psalmist\'s soul itself is greatly dismayed — the inner being, not just the body, is the seat of this profound turmoil, and it drives the anguished cry to God asking how long.\n\n**Isa 28:19** (H2113 ze.va.ah) [M01-D-VCG-01]\n> Isa 28:19 As often as it passes through it will take you; for morning by morning it will pass through , by day and by night ; and it will be sheer terror to understand the message .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Understanding the message of judgment brings sheer terror—grasping its content produces a trembling horror, making comprehension itself terrifying rather than comforting.\n\n**Jer 49:37** (H2865 cha.tat) [M01-D-VCG-02]\n> Jer 49:37 I will terrify Elam before their enemies and before those who seek their life . I will bring disaster upon them, my fierce anger , declares the Lord . I will send the sword after them, until I have consumed them ,\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God will terrify Elam before their enemies, making dismay the inner condition through which he breaks their will; his fierce anger is the divine source of that shattering inner dread.\n\n**Dan 5:6** (H0927 be.hal) [M01-D-VCG-03]\n> Dan 5:6 Then the king\'s color changed , and his thoughts alarmed him; his limbs gave way , and his knees knocked together .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Dismay at the writing on the wall strikes Belshazzar\'s inner person so violently that it changes his color and causes his limbs to give way and his knees to knock—inner terror fully collapses bodily control.\n\n**Deu 28:28** (H8541 tim.ma.hon) [M01-D-VCG-04]\n> Deu 28:28 The Lord will strike you with madness and blindness and confusion of mind ,\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Confusion of mind is a divine curse striking the inner faculty of cognition; the bewilderment disables rational perception and leaves the person unable to make sense of reality.\n\n**Jer 1:17** (H2865 cha.tat) [M01-D-VCG-04]\n> Jer 1:17 But you , dress yourself for work; arise , and say to them everything that I command you. Do not be dismayed by them , lest I dismay you before them.\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Jeremiah is warned not to let dismay at opponents grip him inwardly, with the sobering threat that if he is dismayed before them, God will dismay him before them — fear is thus a contagious inner collapse with real consequences.\n\n**1Sa 14:15** (H2729 cha.rad) [M01-D-VCG-05]\n> 1Sa 14:15 And there was a panic in the camp , in the field , and among all the people . The garrison and even the raiders trembled , the earth quaked , and it became a very great panic .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling spreads through the Philistine garrison as a contagious inner panic; joined by an earthquake, it produces a total collapse of military cohesion described as a great panic.\n\n**Pro 28:22** (H0926 ba.hal) [M01-D-VCG-05]\n> Pro 28:22 A stingy man hastens after wealth and does not know that poverty will come upon him .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The stingy man hastens after wealth in inner agitation, unaware that poverty is coming; the term points to impulsive, rash inner drive rather than outward terror in this verse.\n\n**Jer 49:24** (H7374 re.tet) [M01-D-VCG-05]\n> Jer 49:24 Damascus has become feeble , she turned to flee , and panic seized her; anguish and sorrows have taken hold of her, as of a woman in labor .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Panic seizes Damascus as it turns to flee, gripping it alongside anguish and birth-pangs; the inner experience is sudden, overwhelming, and physically incapacitating, driving flight and helplessness.\n\n**Gen 27:33** (H2731 cha.ra.dah) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Gen 27:33 Then Isaac trembled very violently and said , " Who was it then that hunted game and brought it to me, and I ate it all before you came , and I have blessed him? Yes, and he shall be blessed ."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Isaac\'s great trembling names the intensity of his inner shock when he discovers he has been deceived; the trembling registers the inner disruption caused by the loss of control over the blessing.\n\n**Exo 15:14** (H7264 ra.gaz) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Exo 15:14 The peoples have heard ; they tremble ; pangs have seized the inhabitants of Philistia .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The nations tremble upon hearing of what God did at the sea; the trembling is an involuntary inner and bodily response of dread produced by hearing of overwhelming divine power directed against enemies.\n\n**Exo 15:15** (H7461A ra.ad) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Exo 15:15 Now are the chiefs of Edom dismayed ; trembling seizes the leaders of Moab ; all the inhabitants of Canaan have melted away .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling seizes the leaders of Moab upon hearing of God\'s acts; the trembling is an uncontrollable inner and physical response to news of divine power, paralyzing those who hear it.\n\n**Deu 1:29** (H6206 a.rats) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Deu 1:29 Then I said to you, \'Do not be in dread or afraid of them .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The people are told not to be in dread — the term names the inner, overwhelming terror that grips a person before a feared enemy; here it is prohibited because God himself fights for Israel.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n\n\n### 2.6 Trembling / Fear Made Somatic\n\nTrembling is fear written on the body. When the whole people trembled at Sinai — "on the morning of the third day there were thunders and lightnings and a thick cloud on the mountain and a very loud trumpet blast, so that all the people in the camp trembled" (Exo 19:16) — the shaking was involuntary, the body\'s uncontrolled response to overwhelming divine presence. When Moses stood before the burning bush and God named himself as the God of the patriarchs, the same response came: "Moses trembled and did not dare to look" (Act 7:32). The trembling is the body registering what the inner person cannot contain — it overcomes the person, it is not chosen, it is the outward sign of an inner state at the limit of what the human frame can absorb.\n\nScripture traces this across a wide range of situations: the nations trembling upon hearing of God\'s deeds at the sea (Exo 15:14), kings whose hair bristles at witnessing catastrophic destruction (Eze 27:35), Isaac trembling violently when he grasps the depth of the deception that has just occurred (Gen 27:33). The body in all these cases enacts what the inner person experiences. There is, however, a theologically distinct subset within this characteristic: trembling at God\'s word as a posture of reverent responsiveness. Isaiah 66:2 places it alongside humility and contrition: "he who is humble and contrite in spirit and trembles at my word" — here the trembling is not panic or terror but the body\'s participation in serious, reverential attention to God\'s communication. This double dimension — somatic fear response on one side, reverential bodily attentiveness on the other — is what makes trembling its own characteristic rather than simply a symptom of the others.\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.6 — Trembling / Fear Made Somatic -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Involuntary bodily expression of fear — trembling, shuddering, quivering registering fear in the body. Somatic: body trembles, bones shake, flesh quivers, hair bristles, knees fail as outward sign of inner fear. Involuntary — overcomes the person (cha.rad, Exo 19:16; entromos, Act 7:32; tromos, Mar 16:8). In many meanings, bodily trembling is the only indicator of inner state (Saul 1Sa 28:5; Elihu Job 37:1). Theologically distinctive subset: trembling at God\'s word as inner posture of solemn reverence (cha.red, Isa 66:2; 66:5; Ezr 9:4; 10:3). Double dimension: physical terror response AND reverential responsiveness to the divine word.\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Exo 19:16** (H2729 cha.rad) [M01-E-VCG-01]\n> Exo 19:16 On the morning of the third day there were thunders and lightnings and a thick cloud on the mountain and a very loud trumpet blast , so that all the people in the camp trembled .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The overwhelming sensory phenomena at Sinai — thunder, lightning, thick cloud, loud trumpet — produced involuntary trembling in all the people, a whole-body fear response to divine presence.\n\n**Act 7:32** (G1790 entromos) [M01-E-VCG-01]\n> Act 7:32 \' I am the God of your fathers , the God of Abraham and of Isaac and of Jacob .\' And Moses trembled and did not dare to look .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Moses trembled and did not dare look when confronted with God\'s self-identification, showing that divine holiness produced an involuntary bodily trembling paired with an inner paralysis of will before God.\n\n**Ezr 10:9** (H7460 ra.ad) [M01-E-VCG-02]\n> Ezr 10:9 Then all the men of Judah and Benjamin assembled at Jerusalem within the three days . It was the ninth month , on the twentieth day of the month . And all the people sat in the open square before the house of God , trembling because of this matter and because of the heavy rain .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The assembled people trembled from two sources simultaneously—the moral gravity of the matter of unfaithfulness and the physical distress of heavy rain—showing bodily and inner agitation combined.\n\n**Psa 2:11** (H7461B re.a.dah) [M01-E-VCG-02]\n> Psa 2:11 Serve the Lord with fear , and rejoice with trembling .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling accompanies rejoicing in service to the Lord — the inner state is not terror but a reverent awe that qualifies and tempers the joy of those who approach God.\n\n**Isa 66:2** (H2730 cha.red) [M01-E-VCG-02]\n> Isa 66:2 All these things my hand has made , and so all these things came to be, declares the Lord . But this is the one to whom I will look : he who is humble and contrite in spirit and trembles at my word .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling at God\'s word is paired with humility and a contrite spirit as the inner posture God looks for; the trembling is located in the spirit and shows reverence that orients the whole inner person toward God\'s communication.\n\n**Job 18:20** (H8178A sa.ar) [M01-E-VCG-03]\n> Job 18:20 They of the west are appalled at his day , and horror seizes them of the east .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Witnesses east and west shudder with horror at the wicked man\'s fate, showing shuddering as a visceral, full-body inner response to witnessing catastrophic divine judgment.\n\n**Eze 26:16** (H2729 cha.rad) [M01-E-VCG-03]\n> Eze 26:16 Then all the princes of the sea will step down from their thrones and remove their robes and strip off their embroidered garments . They will clothe themselves with trembling ; they will sit on the ground and tremble every moment and be appalled at you .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling seizes the sea-princes at Tyre\'s fall so completely that they clothe themselves with it—it becomes like a garment, an all-enveloping inner and bodily state produced by witnessing catastrophic destruction.\n\n**Eze 27:35** (H8175A sa.ar) [M01-E-VCG-03]\n> Eze 27:35 All the inhabitants of the coastlands are appalled at you, and the hair of their kings bristles with horror ; their faces are convulsed .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Shuddering is so intense at Tyre\'s destruction that kings\' hair bristles—the inner horror of witnessing the city\'s ruin produces an involuntary physical reaction that overrides composure and dignity.\n\n**Gen 27:33** (H2731 cha.ra.dah) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Gen 27:33 Then Isaac trembled very violently and said , " Who was it then that hunted game and brought it to me, and I ate it all before you came , and I have blessed him? Yes, and he shall be blessed ."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Isaac\'s great trembling names the intensity of his inner shock when he discovers he has been deceived; the trembling registers the inner disruption caused by the loss of control over the blessing.\n\n**Exo 15:14** (H7264 ra.gaz) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Exo 15:14 The peoples have heard ; they tremble ; pangs have seized the inhabitants of Philistia .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The nations tremble upon hearing of what God did at the sea; the trembling is an involuntary inner and bodily response of dread produced by hearing of overwhelming divine power directed against enemies.\n\n**Exo 15:15** (H7461A ra.ad) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Exo 15:15 Now are the chiefs of Edom dismayed ; trembling seizes the leaders of Moab ; all the inhabitants of Canaan have melted away .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling seizes the leaders of Moab upon hearing of God\'s acts; the trembling is an uncontrollable inner and physical response to news of divine power, paralyzing those who hear it.\n\n**Deu 1:29** (H6206 a.rats) [M01-E-VCG-04]\n> Deu 1:29 Then I said to you, \'Do not be in dread or afraid of them .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The people are told not to be in dread — the term names the inner, overwhelming terror that grips a person before a feared enemy; here it is prohibited because God himself fights for Israel.\n\n**Deu 28:65** (H7268 rag.gaz) [M01-E-VCG-05]\n> Deu 28:65 And among these nations you shall find no respite , and there shall be no resting place for the sole of your foot , but the Lord will give you there a trembling heart and failing eyes and a languishing soul .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ A trembling heart is given by God as a curse in exile—an unceasing inner agitation that denies rest, paired with failing eyes and a languishing soul, describing total inner collapse.\n\n**Job 21:6** (H6427 pal.la.tsut) [M01-E-VCG-05]\n> Job 21:6 When I remember , I am dismayed , and shuddering seizes my flesh .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Shuddering takes hold of Job\'s flesh the moment memory brings dismay, showing the physical dimension of inner terror as the body involuntarily enacts what the mind perceives.\n\n**Eze 12:18** (H7269 rog.zah) [M01-E-VCG-05]\n> Eze 12:18 " Son of man , eat your bread with quaking , and drink water with trembling and with anxiety .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Quivering accompanies drinking water, showing that inner agitation has become so pervasive it manifests in the body during the most ordinary acts of daily survival.\n\n**Hos 13:1** (H7578 re.tet) [M01-E-VCG-05]\n> Hos 13:1 When Ephraim spoke , there was trembling ; he was exalted in Israel , but he incurred guilt through Baal and died .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ When Ephraim spoke, trembling was the response of others, indicating a former authoritative presence that inspired awe; this inner-commanding stature was then lost through idolatry and spiritual death.\n\n**Phili 2:12** (G5156 tromos) [M01-E-VCG-06]\n> Phili 2:12 Therefore , my beloved , as you have always obeyed , so now , not only as in my presence but much more in my absence , work out your own salvation with fear and trembling ,\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Trembling accompanies fear as the inner-bodily tone of serious, awed engagement with one\'s own salvation, indicating that working out salvation demands earnest gravity rather than casual ease.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n\n\n### 2.7 Anticipatory Dread and Anxiety\n\nAnticipatory dread is fear that lives in the future. It is not triggered by what is happening now but by what is coming — what is imagined, foreknown, or feared will arrive. Ezekiel conveys its pervasiveness: anxiety so saturates the inner person that "eat your bread with quaking, and drink water with trembling and with anxiety" (Eze 12:18) — it has colonised every moment of life, infiltrating even the most ordinary acts. Deuteronomy names it as a covenantal curse: "Night and day you shall be in dread and have no assurance of your life" (Deu 28:66) — the chronicity is the punishment, an unrelenting inner burden with no relief. Job describes the interior structure of it: "For the thing that I fear comes upon me, and what I dread befalls me" (Job 3:25) — he had carried the anticipation before the event arrived, and the dread and the loss converge. The New Testament adds the register of judgment: Hebrews describes the person who sins deliberately after receiving the truth as facing "a fearful expectation of judgment, and a fury of fire that will consume the adversaries" (Heb 10:27). This anticipatory dread of divine judgment is a rational, forward-looking fear directed toward what is real and certain for those who persist in willful rejection.\n\nWhat distinguishes anticipatory dread from acute fear and alarm is temporal structure: acute fear is a response to what is immediately present; anticipatory dread weighs on the person before the threatening thing arrives, sometimes long before. And where acute fear may pass with the moment, anticipatory dread can become chronic — a sustained burden that reshapes the whole character of a life.\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.7 — Anticipatory Dread and Anxiety -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Sustained, forward-looking inner burden of dread — fear not triggered by immediate present threat but by what is anticipated, imagined, or foreknown. Chronicity and anticipation: weighs down the heart as ongoing burden (de.a.gah, Pro 12:25), saturates every moment (Eze 12:18-19), unrelenting day and night (pa.chad, Deu 28:66-67), anticipatory anguish preceding and matching the feared event (Job 3:25). Includes fear of death as lifelong enslaving burden (fobos, Heb 2:15), fearful expectation of judgment (foberos, Heb 10:27), conscientious dread of divine accountability shaping pastoral conduct (2Cor 12:20; Gal 4:11).\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Gen 9:2** (H4172B mo.ra) [M01-A-VCG-07]\n> Gen 9:2 The fear of you and the dread of you shall be upon every beast of the earth and upon every bird of the heavens , upon everything that creeps on the ground and all the fish of the sea . Into your hand they are delivered .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fear directed toward humans is placed upon every creature as a permanent condition; it shapes animals\' inner response to mankind, producing avoidance and submission.\n\n**Deu 4:34** (H4172A mo.rah) [M01-A-VCG-07]\n> Deu 4:34 Or has any god ever attempted to go and take a nation for himself from the midst of another nation , by trials , by signs , by wonders , and by war , by a mighty hand and an outstretched arm , and by great deeds of terror , all of which the Lord your God did for you in Egypt before your eyes ?\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God\'s great deeds of terror in Egypt are acts that overwhelm the will — the term names the fear-inspiring power displayed through wonders and war that demonstrated God\'s unmatched authority over nations.\n\n**Gen 9:2** (H2844A chat) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Gen 9:2 The fear of you and the dread of you shall be upon every beast of the earth and upon every bird of the heavens , upon everything that creeps on the ground and all the fish of the sea . Into your hand they are delivered .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror is an instilled inner disposition placed upon all animals toward humanity after the flood, making every creature fear humans as a divinely ordered reality.\n\n**Psa 55:4** (H0367 e.mah) [M01-C-VCG-04]\n> Psa 55:4 My heart is in anguish within me; the terrors of death have fallen upon me .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Terror is located in the heart — the terrors of death fall upon the psalmist, causing inner anguish so intense it is felt as a physical collapse within the chest.\n\n**Psa 94:19** (H8312 sar.ap.pim) [M01-F-VCG-01]\n> Psa 94:19 When the cares of my heart are many , your consolations cheer my soul .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Anxious cares multiply within the heart, but God\'s consolations restore the soul — the anxiety is located in the heart as a crowding inner burden that divine comfort directly counters.\n\n**Eze 12:18** (H1674 de.a.gah) [M01-F-VCG-01]\n> Eze 12:18 " Son of man , eat your bread with quaking , and drink water with trembling and with anxiety .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Anxiety so saturates the inner person that even the basic acts of eating and drinking cannot be done without it—it is a constant, pervasive inner dread that accompanies every moment of existence.\n\n**Job 3:25** (H3025 ya.gor) [M01-F-VCG-02]\n> Job 3:25 For the thing that I fear comes upon me, and what I dread befalls me .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Job names a dreaded thing that already sat within him as an anticipated fear, and that dread has now materialized into reality—showing fear as an inner anticipatory anguish preceding loss.\n\n**Psa 34:4** (H4034 me.go.rah) [M01-F-VCG-02]\n> Psa 34:4 I sought the Lord , and he answered me and delivered me from all my fears .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ The psalmist sought the Lord and was delivered from all his fears — these fears were the inner terrors and anxieties that had gripped him, and divine response removed them entirely.\n\n**Isa 66:4** (H4035 me.gu.rah) [M01-F-VCG-02]\n> Isa 66:4 I also will choose harsh treatment for them and bring their fears upon them, because when I called , no one answered , when I spoke , they did not listen ; but they did what was evil in my eyes and chose that in which I did not delight ."\n_Meaning of the term here:_ God will bring upon the disobedient the very fears they harbored; the inner anxieties and dreads are treated as consequences fitting their rejection of God, turning their own fears into the instrument of judgment.\n\n**Deu 28:66** (H6342 pa.chad) [M01-F-VCG-03]\n> Deu 28:66 Your life shall hang in doubt before you. Night and day you shall be in dread and have no assurance of your life .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Continual dread without assurance of life is a covenantal curse; the inner experience is unrelenting, consuming both night and day, with no relief or certainty of survival.\n\n**Heb 10:27** (G5398 foberos) [M01-F-VCG-04]\n> Heb 10:27 but a fearful expectation of judgment , and a fury of fire that will consume the adversaries .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fearful expectation of judgment is the inner experience awaiting those who sin willfully after receiving truth—an anticipatory dread lodged in the mind directed toward coming fiery condemnation.\n\n**2Cor 12:20** (G5399 fobeō) [M01-F-VCG-05]\n> 2Cor 12:20 For I fear that perhaps when I come I may find you not as I wish , and that you may find me not as you wish — that perhaps there may be quarreling , jealousy , anger , hostility , slander , gossip , conceit , and disorder .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Paul\'s fear is an anticipatory dread rooted in thought about what he may find—relational disorder and sin—engaging the mind with anxious expectation before the visit even happens.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n\n\n### 2.8 Timidity and Cowardly Shrinking\n\nTimidity is fear evaluated as failure. The other forms of fear in this study are, for the most part, described as things that happen to the inner person — states that arise, overwhelm, press in from outside, or build over time. Timidity is different: it is what the inner person ought not to have, a disposition that stands in the place where faith and courage should be. When the disciples panicked in the storm and Jesus asked "Why are you afraid, O you of little faith?" (Mat 8:26), he linked cowardly recoiling directly to a failure of trust. The alarm they felt was not the problem; that alarm was acute fear meeting a threatening situation. What he named was the inner collapse that should have been held by trust in his presence with them. Paul makes the constitutional dimension explicit: "God gave us a spirit not of fear but of power and love and self-control" (2Ti 1:7). Timidity is identified as a spirit-level disposition that God has not implanted — it is an absence at the inner foundation, a deficiency of constitution rather than a response to circumstances. The contrast makes it clear: where the given spirit produces power, love, and self-discipline, timidity produces recoiling, withdrawal, and ultimately apostasy. Revelation 21:8 places the cowardly alongside idolaters and murderers as those who have not endured — it is the person who shrank under pressure rather than stood.\n\nThe command against it is direct. Jesus says in John 14:27: "Let not your hearts be troubled, neither let them be afraid" — the will is addressed, because timidity is a disposition the will can refuse. This distinguishes it from all the other characteristics in this study, which are not primarily addressed as choices. Timidity alone is consistently presented as what the inner person must not yield to, and faith as the created disposition that displaces it.\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.8 — Timidity and Cowardly Shrinking -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Fear as inner failure of constitution — cowardly, faithless recoiling presented as moral and spiritual defect. Evaluative: unlike M01-B (natural alarm) or M01-F (burden), timidity here is what the inner person ought not to have — a disposition that should yield to faith and courage. 2Ti 1:7 (deilia): explicitly named as spirit-level disposition God has not implanted, deficiency of inner constitution. Joh 14:27 (deiliaō): commanded not to yield to cowardly shrinking. Rev 21:8 (deilos): cowardice listed with idolatry and murder as vices of the lake of fire — apostasy under pressure. Pro 29:25 (cha.ra.dah): fear of man named as inner trap that ensnares the person. Not simply fear being present — fear evaluated as opposite of faith, trust, inner integrity.\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Mat 8:26** (G1169 deilos) [M01-G-VCG-01]\n> Mat 8:26 And he said to them , " Why are you afraid , O you of little faith ?" Then he rose and rebuked the winds and the sea , and there was a great calm .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Jesus names the disciples\' panic in the storm as timidity, linking it directly to little faith—their inner cowardice in the face of danger reveals a failure of trust in him who was present with them.\n\n**Joh 14:27** (G1168 deiliaō) [M01-G-VCG-01]\n> Joh 14:27 Peace I leave with you ; my peace I give to you . Not as the world gives do I give to you . Let not your hearts be troubled , neither let them be afraid .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Jesus contrasts his given peace with an inner timidity or cowardly shrinking, commanding the heart not to yield to that fearful recoiling, positioning the will against such inner collapse.\n\n**2Ti 1:7** (G1167 deilia) [M01-G-VCG-01]\n> 2Ti 1:7 for God gave us a spirit not of fear but of power and love and self-control .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Timidity is contrasted with the spirit God gives—power, love, and self-control; it is identified as a spirit-level disposition that God has not implanted, making it a failure of inner constitution rather than circumstance.\n\n<!-- /EVIDENCE -->\n'

The full profile of each characteristic is established in Chapter 2 — your chapter does not re-establish them, only refers to them by the characteristic name as you see them here.\n\n- **Reverential Fear / Fear of God as Governing Orientation** — Fear-of-God as enduring inner orientation rather than reactive event — the constitutive disposition that governs the whole inner life: informing conduct, motivating worship, grounding covenant relationship, forming identity.\n- **Acute Fear and Alarm** — Reactive, situational fear — sudden inner state of alarm, dread, or terror triggered by specific threat, unexpected encounter, supernatural appearance, or display of divine/extraordinary power.\n- **Boundary — Terms Held for Researcher Decision** — Terms with empty meaning corpora (all verses set aside, no Pass A meanings) OR with analytical questions unresolved in Phase 3.\n- **Terror as Overwhelming Force** — Terror characterised as active, assaulting force — something that comes upon the inner person from outside, encircles them, pursues them, or is projected by one power onto another.\n- **Dismay and Inner Collapse** — Sudden dissolution of inner coherence — what happens to the inner person when shock, catastrophe, or overwhelming news shatters composure and disables capacity to function.\n- **Trembling / Fear Made Somatic** — Involuntary bodily expression of fear — trembling, shuddering, quivering registering fear in the body.\n- **Anticipatory Dread and Anxiety** — Sustained, forward-looking inner burden of dread — fear not triggered by immediate present threat but by what is anticipated, imagined, or foreknown.\n- **Timidity and Cowardly Shrinking** — Fear as inner failure of constitution — cowardly, faithless recoiling presented as moral and spiritual defect.\n\n---\n\n## 2. The characteristics in this study\n\nScripture\'s vocabulary for fear, dread and terror organises into seven distinct inner-life characteristics — each a different way the inner person receives, registers, or is governed by the encounter with power, threat, or divine holiness — together with a group of related terms that support the evidence but do not themselves constitute fully established inner-being characteristics.\n\n### 2.1 Reverential Fear / Fear of God as Governing Orientation\n\nReverential fear is not a feeling that comes and goes — it is the disposition that shapes a life. Scripture returns again and again to fear of God as the inner orientation that orders everything else: the way a person conducts themselves, the basis on which they receive God\'s guidance, the inner restraint that makes exploitation unthinkable, the relational posture that opens the way to covenant knowledge. Proverbs names it as foundational: "The fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge; fools despise wisdom and instruction" (Pro 1:7). This is not fear as anxiety or alarm but fear as structured reverence — a stable inner orientation toward God as the supreme reality, worthy of awe, before whom the whole person stands accountable. The fear of God is learnable, transmissible from one generation to another, and, as Jeremiah makes plain, capable of being implanted by God himself deep within the person. Its absence is equally diagnostic: "the fear of me is not in you, declares the Lord God of hosts" — Jeremiah identifies its absence as the inner root of Israel\'s apostasy (Jer 2:19). Where this characteristic lives, it governs; where it is absent, the inner person drifts toward whatever replaces it.\n\nWhat distinguishes reverential fear from the other forms of fear in this study is precisely its stability and its direction. It is not a reactive episode triggered by threat or shock — that is acute fear and alarm. It is not the body\'s involuntary trembling — that is fear made somatic. Reverential fear is the enduring orientation of the heart toward God, the constitutive stance from which the whole inner life takes its bearings. Psalm 25:14 captures the intimate consequence: "The friendship of the Lord is for those who fear him, and he makes known to them his covenant."\n\n<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch2 §2.1 — Reverential Fear / Fear of God as Governing Orientation -->\n\n**Sub-group description (from analytical record):**\n\n> Fear-of-God as enduring inner orientation rather than reactive event — the constitutive disposition that governs the whole inner life: informing conduct, motivating worship, grounding covenant relationship, forming identity. Rooted across hundreds of verses: fear of God as the root of obedience (Deu 6:2; 10:12), criterion for divine guidance (Psa 25:12; 111:5; 34:7), foundation of wisdom (Pro 1:7; 9:10), restraining force on cruelty and injustice (Lev 19:14; 25:17; 25:43), defining character of the righteous (Job 1:1; Neh 7:2). NT: motivating awe governing obedience to Christ and authorities (Col 3:22; Eph 5:21; 1Pe 1:17; 2:17). Learnable, transmissible, divinely implantable; its absence marks moral blindness.\n\n**Key verses for this characteristic:**\n\n**Lev 19:14** (H3372H ya.re) [M01-A-VCG-01]\n> Lev 19:14 You shall not curse the deaf or put a stumbling block before the blind , but you shall fear your God : I am the Lord .\n_Meaning of the term here:_ Fearing God is the inner constraint that prevents exploiting the vulnerable — the prohibition against harming the deaf and blind is backed not by human oversight but by God-directed reverence within the person.\n\n**Jer 2:19** (H6345 pach.dah) [M01-A-VCG-01]\n> Jer 2:19 Your evil will chastise you, and your apostasy will reprove you.
